RATING: 9
Superb game - densely thematic with just the right mix of luck and strategy.

The races complement each other nicely and each has a distinct feel. It would have been easy for FFG to release each team as an expansion but with 6 in the box there is a lot of immediate depth.

A bit of a shame it loses the "spatial" aspect of BB with the long-throws etc, but it captures the campaign feel perfectly.

RATING: 9
This game plays like a more violent Balloon Cup in that there's a tug of war over several cards at once.  I need to play some more to see how all the cards can work together, but I like it a lot so far.

AFTER FOUR PLAYS: This has become my favorite game from 2011.  With four players, it can be a little long, but it flies with two, and it's a very different experience.  None of the races seem overbalanced (I'm 4-0 and have played four different teams).  Hoping for some good expansions in the future!

RATING: 6
Sokat gondolkodtam két pontszám közt, végül a kevesebbet adtam rá, de ez még javulhat. Egy schotten-totten-re emlékeztető játék, csak bonyolultabb, és elég hosszú lehet. Itt amerikai foci-meccseket kell megnyerni, amik párhozamosan zajlanak, illetve néha több résztvevős torna is zajlik pluszban ezek mellett, ahol egyszerre 2-nél több csapat is küzdhet a győzelemért. Aki sorra kerül, az lepakol valamelyik meccshez vagy tornához egy játékost a saját oldalára, erősítve ezzel az ottani csapatát. Az új csapattag típusától függően üthet, labdát megszerezhet, csalhat, cserélhet, egy meccs vagy torna győztese pedig növelheti nézőszámát (=győzelmi pont), új sztárokat igazolhat, illetve mindenféle segítő kártyákat szerezhet. Általában a vesztesek is kapnak vigaszdíjat. Nagyon változatos a sok kártya miatt, de ami az előnye, az kicsit a hátránya is szerintem... Nekem a vége felé már túl sok volt a magunk elé lepakolt kártya, esélytelennek éreztem átlátni, hogy ki milyen módosítókat tud használni. Emellett kár hogy ennyire nyelvfüggő, illetve hosszú. Az előírt 5 kör 3 fővel közel 2 óra volt... De mindenképp előnye, hogy 2-3-4 fővel is játszható.

RATING: 7
I was a huge fan of Blood Bowl, since its 2nd edition. Today I have not enough time to play in a league, so I don't really play it anymore since the single game is less satisfying than playing a series of matches with the players increasing their skills...
With this background, I was eager to try BBTM. Well, the game is a fun ride! Everything is quite simple and straightforward, but is also quite thematic. There's lots of luck, of course, but the fast and furious play makes up for the somewhat random feel... The teams play very differently, and there's even quite a bit of interplay variability due to the removed cards.
In the end, if you don't take this game very seriously, you can expect buckets of fun from it!!

RATING: 7.5

This is not Blood Bowl, but rather a fairly simple card game where you try to out think your opponent by trying to win hands on opposite sides of the table in order to upgrade your team to gain the most victory points at the end.  You are a manager of one of many different factions from Warhammer with unique powers making every team slightly different thus different strategies required to win.  I like it a lot.

RATING: 9
Better with 3 players, with 4 it takes a bit long for what it is.  I'm sure 2 player is good too, but I think I like this as a semi-light, social game.

Everyone we've played it with likes it.  Even non-boardgamers.

Note: If only one manager has players in a highlight, he gets EVERYTHING on the card!  An incentive to injure!

Fun, somewhat light, but nevertheless there was some definite thinking going on.  Deciding how to commit when you want to Sprint to get rid of a Lineman is interesting, etc.  Sufficient time for trash-talk, but maybe I should've spent more time thinking since several players (myself included) did slow the game down by thinking on their turns.

A bit long for what it is (but enjoyable throughout.)  A definite element of luck. Finally, it can be easy to miss/forget the Team Upgrade abilities of the other coaches.

RATING: 7
Kicsomagolás és alkatrészek:
A doboz méretének semmi köze bármilyen szabványhoz és a minősége is ócska vékony papír ami nagyon hamar elszakadhat. Ez így nem egy FFG minőség. Viszont a grafika tetszetős. Kibontás után a szabály alatt egy 2 db kinyomó karton leledzik, mely nem értem miért van fóliában. E mögött van a tároló rekesz, mely egy kétszínű grafikával van nyomtatva. Itt található három kártyapakli, két dobókocka és összeszerelő alkatrészek.
A kártyák grafikái szépek, de a kártyák szélein sorja leledzik. Erősen javasolom a kártyavédőket, legalább a csapatkártyákra. A dobókocka sajnos műanyag, mely asztalon dobáskor nagyon hangos.
A kinyomó kartonból könnyen kiszedhetők az elemek és a minősége kiváló mind grafika mind pedig anyagminőség szempontjából. Sajnos nem fényesek, azaz nincs rajtuk  felületi védelem, így kopásesélyesek.
A játékos kártyák hajszálpontosan illeszkednek a Swam 57x90 kártyavédőkbe, de a kis kártyák 41-es méretűek, még nem találtam hozzá normális védőt.
Az pontjelző alkatrészek könnyen összeszerelhetők voltak és jól működnek.

Játék:
Leültem, megtanították és megnyert engem a játék. Nem vagyok se foci se fantasy rajongó, de mégis úgy tetszik a játék ahogy van. Nagy csatákat lehet benne vívni és ha nem agyalják túl a köröket még pörgős is. Ajánlott darab, aki szereti a kártyás játékokat. Szerintem nyelvfüggetlenné lehetett volna tenni.

RATING: 7.5
Was very excited to try this game. Got to play someones copy at an FLGS game night. 

4 player game. Was very, very enjoyable! Had all of us cheering and booing. Took about 2.5 hours (all of us new, and sort of knew the rules). Would play again in  a heartbeat, but did move down my wishlist ranks. 

Notes: 
[-] Tons of pieces that need organization (several card and token types), making setup and take down a little obnoxious for the weight of the game. 
[-] Not much depth (although it is a light-medium game). Match rewards and player match-up choices are interesting. Asymmetry between teams is there, but not super noticeable after one game. 
[+] Interactive. I think this game is best with 3-4 players. 2 seems like it would be kind of boring, but 4 did make the game last a lot longer (especially considering the game weight). 

I really like this game a lot, but I just do not see it fitting into my normal rotation. Rarely are my groups 3-4, and it actually took longer than expected for the weight of the game in my opinion (although I can see that decreasing slightly after experience. It is still somewhat lengthy to play with the standard round rules). Depth wise, I would predict that this game would get stale for my tastes rather quickly. I would like it for my collection at some point, but I think it would only get played under perfect circumstances (player amount, mood, and desire for heavier game). Will still consider this for a future purchases.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Juego de cartas ambientado en warhammer y basado en el famoso (y aún no por mí probado) Blood Bowl. Cada jugador es un manager de equipo. La partida dura cuatro turnos y en cada turno se pone en juego un torneo y cuatro crónicas de partido. En un turno, un jugador juega seis cartas que va colocando junto a la carta de torneo/crónica en el lado que más le convenga (cada lado supone unos premios, en caso de ganar). Al final del turno se comparan los valores de las cartas a ambos lados y el que más puntos consiga es el que gana y se lleva el premio (el de su lado más el premio central). El perdedor se lleva también un premio de consolación.

Las habilidades de los jugadores son variadas y los puntos que aportan al resultado del encuentro pueden verse alterados por varios factores (el hecho de haber sido derribado, haber hecho trampas).

Entre los premios hay cartas de equipo, cartas de poder o cartas de extrellas (jugadores con mejores características).

Es un juego sencillo de jugar y de explicar, pero con un grado de profundidad suficiente para hacerlo muy interesante. Recomendable.

RATING: 4
Reminds me of an Americanized Condottiere. All pay auctions (like Condottiere), but with post-decision random elements and special powers on some of the cards.

It's hard to take the game seriously, though. Not because of the art or theme, but because of the cheating chits. They make predicting outcomes pretty tough, even if half the time they help and one fifth of the time they hurt. Without the ability to predict what will happen based off of your decisions, it's tough to invest in those decisions.

It's fairly quick. So it has that going for it.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Take that, BattleLine!

I dig this game, but I definitely have to be in the mood for a take that game to want to play it. It's really good for the type of game it is. I just tend to not want to play things that feel so... reactionary all the time.

The flavor is a lot of fun. The variety of teams is super cool. You always have fewer cards than you want, which gives the game some nice tension.

The setup time is sort of a pain. It's not awful, but it does prevent this from being just a simple quick playing game like BL where you can knock a few games out pretty fast if nobody is prone to AP.

Compared to BL though it just... lacks an elegance. There's some fiddliness that just doesn't exist in BL. BattleLine also has better opportunity for long-term strategy. In this you tend to feel totally screwed if you have to change direction mid-play, whereas in BL it doesn't sting as much, it feels like you can save yourself more through strategic plays rather than just giving up and accepting the consolation prize. In particular, this makes it feel like luck of the draw is a bigger factor here. It might actually not be since here, at least, the luck is all up front every round, but when your opponent just has a hand you can't do anything about you really FEEL the luck.

Overall, it's a fun time. BL is too dry and themeless for you, check this out for sure. However if you prefer more interesting strategy and don't mind an abstract feel, I feel BL is a superior game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
I used to play the full version of Blood Bowl back in the day. FWIW, this game has almost no similarity to that title aside from the theme. In reality, this is a cross between German fare like Battle Line and American take-that style card play and dice rolling.

Players each have a hand of players that have a value between 1-4 starting, and 0-2? once they're tackled. Players also have various attributes like being dirty, being able to tackle, or being able to pick up the ball. Each round a number of pitches are set out that give rewards for having the most points allocated to them. The goal is to just collect VPs.

In practice the game plays like this: I play a card to a field and pick up the ball. My opponent plays a card of their own and tries to tackle me, which is a 50/50 die roll. If I'm tackled, my card is worth fewer points. We do this a few times and at the end of the round, the players with the dirty chits on them (some of the teams have a lot of players who get these random chits when they're played, others don't) can be a boon, granting extra points to their value, or a liability, as they can be tossed unexpectedly.

Really, this unpredictability is why I think a lot of German game fans will despise this game. There are a lot of random factors to mitigate. You don't know if a tackle is going to work, you don't know if that cheating chit is going to win a fight over a given pitch or assure your defeat...&c.

I don't mind random elements in shorter games like this. If played briskly I wouldn't object to it strenuously, though for my money vaguely similar fare like Titan: The Arena is considerably more desirable as it has the same sort of card play without the egregiously random elements of this title. If this runs over 60 minutes it's taking far too long though.

Needs a squig expansion.

RATING: 10
I've played this game now more than 20 times.

I have the Sudden Death and Foul Play expansions.

I've played quite a few card based games and pretty much disliked them all. I tried this game expecting it to be just *meh* but ended up loving it and proving to me that card based board games can be fun.

Despite the apparent imbalance of the teams and rampant chaos in this game it still somehow almost always boils down to a close victory. The plays are very different and you never know exactly what will happen so you will either have to make a bet or play safe. Both strategies work and I love this aspect of the game.

I've read quite a few discussions on the forum about the imbalance of teams or how some of the are easier to play than others. This is acceptable to me and doesn't diminish the playing experience. You can draw a very good team and still lose or you can pick one of the weaker teams and win by a large margin. This game is heavy on the luck factor and some people might dislike that, but hey, this is Blood Bowl! When the referee is down you are supposed to bring out the chainsaws and order your hired wizard to throw in a fireball.

Cons:
- Can suffer from leader bashing. The Sudden Death expansion and the random contracts help with this.
- Base game teams can be a little bland after the addition of the teams in the expansions.

RATING: 7
[2012-08-27 Rating: n.a. -> 7]

Blood Bowl: Team Manager (BBTM) reminds me a little bit of Schotten Totten (or Battle Line if you want). Commit one of your player to a match-up, wait for the response of your opponents and see if you can win the match-up in the end.

What I do really like is your ability to kind of shape your own team strategy. While every team has it's default strengths and weaknesses, you can try to compensate or strengthen your team's characteristics by acquiring new players or upgrades. This gives BBTM a nice feeling of progression.

Another thing I believe BBTM gets right is it's theme. Sure, it not like this is a substitute for a full blown game of Blood Bowl, but the feeling isn't too far from it and it plays in less time. Something which matters more and more at this point in my life. 

Sadly, there are is one thing that prevents the game to get a higher rating: Luck. Normally, I don't mind luck in games, but somehow it bothers me here. Some of the upgrades that give you points in the end game scoring are just a little too strong in my oppinion. And there is no way you can be sure you will see one of it. [Edit: FFG seems to have addressed this point in the FAQ. Here, those powerful cards are removed from the game and are only used in a variant. I need to try the game again without them.]

RATING: 8
Pretty decent concept that manages to capture the theme of playing in a Blood Bowl season.   Star Players are added to your roster, and staff and team upgrades are available.   It plays sort of like an homage to Battle Line as players will compete in several different matches each week, trying to have the most strength on your side of the field.   The game is typical FFG in that there is component sprawl and a lot of table clutter.   A refined game this is not.   But, it's not that complicated either.  Due the to luck of cheating tokens and die rolls, it doesn't pay to over-analyze your options.   Quick players will make for a better experience.   And it is better with 2 or 3 players, as opposed to 4.  All in all, it is better than I expected.  And it is fairly priced, which is a welcome change of pace for FFG.   

(bumping rating from 7 to 8 after many plays.  There are some Staff cards that need to be removed per the 'No Salary Cap' FAQ.  Also, the ability to play 4 rounds instead of 5 or 6 is a useful variant.)

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I'll start with the bad:

Like many other Fantasy Flight Game, this game comes as no surprise - it isn't balanced at all. Skaven are the most overpowered of all the 6 races in the box (they have a team upgrade card that gives you 2 victory points even when you loose a match - if you get it early in the game, you will win no matter what). After them, all the races that have an arrow sign on players (wood elves - the most) are in big advantage, because they can escape placing guardians (they litterally don't do anything). Worst are chaos and dwarves, both of which are dependent upon random factor, which might give you something, but can kick your players out (6/36, or was it 6/30 chance, I'm not 100% sure) - in that case, you loose match almost for sure. Also, dwarves (absolute worst) are the only race that don't start with big guy, and I don't see any advantage that would negate that disadvantage. Oh, don't forget their team upgrades - they are also the worst, because they need some conditions to work, and even then, bonuses they give are poor compared to other team's team upgrades (which, I repeat, usually don't need any condition to be met). Orcs and humans are something in-between: orcs have some dependace on luck, but that is balanced out in skills they have, and one of the stronger team upgrades. Human's biggest advantage is that they don't have any major disadvantage. They are true masters of being something in-between.

But then the good:

Our group usually have a lot of funny moments playing this one out. Blood Bowl (normal version), is my absolute favorite game, so it comes as no surprise that I love this one too - it doesn't have all those tactics that Blood Bowl (normal version) has, but it plays quickly, and it can be played by 4 people at the same time (it could be played even in more players if you really want to... you just need something that will represent 1 or 2 more football token). It is great as a filler game. Especially if your group is going to play a game for >4 players, and you are waiting for some of the group members to come.

RATING: 6
2015-05-07 : Well-designed pure Ameritrash game which manages (ahum) to compact a Blood Bowl season down to its essentials while keeping the flavour of the various teams intact. 

We played it 4-player and this has the disadvantage that you can't remodel your team for a specific opponent. If you get the choice between 2 star players, one of which works against the Dark Elves and one against the Skaven, which one do you pick if you might encounter either or none of them in the next match ? You really don't need any additional random elements in a game like this ..

A point is deducted from the score because of the decision to use font size 3 (or whatever) on the cards, the failure to put important abilities like "dodge" or "sure hands" as a big icon on them and the color palette of different teams being too similar.

RATING: 6
In Blood Bowl Team Manager, players will be playing one of 6 unique teams.  Each player will commit players from their teams to various matches (tournaments and highlights) which contain benefits for placing players there and benefits you compete for.  Some benefits are better players, some are general upgrades, some are team specific upgrades, and finally you can gain fans (which are basically VP in the game).  In highlights, only two teams can take part but all players may participate in the tournaments.  So, I definitely consider this game to be more fun with 3 or 4 players than with two.  This is especially so because some teams play better against others.  Overall, it's a fun but not too complex ameritrash card game with a wonderful theme that truly shines.  There's quite a lot of excitement with the dice rolling and revealing of cheating tokens.  It should be noted that there is an issue with some of the Staff Upgrade cards which is highlighted here:

http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/768304/faq-is-out

In the end, I found it to be a bit longer than I would have liked with 3/4 people and can't compete with other 2 player games I've played.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4

I miss a lot of the humor because I like thinking about the moves, etc.

Again, I think this trick taking game is well done and clever, just not for me.

RATING: 7
There are a number of games where players duke it out in a tug-of-war of some sort (e.g. Battle Line), and special powers aren't uncommon, either (Caesar & Cleopatra, Ruse & Bruise) but I don't think I've seen an implementation so far that manages to create a thematically dense game and doesn't at the same time descend into pure chaos, especially with more than two players.

Simply dividing the conflict into a number of smaller battlegrounds goes a long way to containing that chaos because that way you don't need to put all your eggs in one basket. Oh, luck still plays a major role, and you can come out of a round badly bruised through no particular fault of your own but it rarely feels like there was nothing you could do, and in any case, the blow is often softened by not all spoils going to the victor.

If you can handle a bit of chaos, and the theme appeals just a little bit, give it a try. It's quite likely not as good with just two players, though.

RATING: 8
I was a fan of the original Bloodbowl and I was pleasantly surprised of how well the theme was evoked in this "manager" card version.

Beside the theme (which my wife was not into, for example), the game play is excellent and clever, with a few original twists on solid mechanics (card placement and numerical value, but with a few rules which transmit the feeling of a football match, with control of the ball and "tackling" other players).

Really an excellent implementation.

I warmly suggest it to anyone who liked bloodbowl and/or to anyone who likes card-interaction games with strongly different starting positions and asymmetrical powers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blood Bowl Team Manager is a card game with a very smooth Euro-like core, plus a generous helping of the sort of aggression and thematic color you'd expect from its Fantasy Flight and Games Workshop pedigree. Each player chooses a team such as Dwarves, Elves, Skaven, etc. Each team has its own unique deck of player cards, and also a unique set of upgrades that can be added between matches. Powerful "Star Player" cards can also be added to the deck, although I wouldn't principally describe BBTM as a deck-building game.

The goal of BBTM is to earn the most fans for your team by the end of the game. Fans can be earned by making cool/illegal plays, meeting goals set by some of your upgrade cards, and most importantly, by entering (and hopefully winning) matches and tournaments. Most matches involve only two teams, and you do have some choice over who you will be playing against. The tournaments are multi-team brawls.

The basic game flow consists of taking turns committing player cards to one of the two or three matches your team is playing that round. The players each have a basic strength value, along with one or more special powers and/or action icons. The special powers could be just about anything. The action icons include cheating, tackling other players, gaining possession of the ball, and drawing more cards from your deck. Tackles involve rolling dice in an attempt to reduce an opposing player's effectiveness (and maybe make him lose control of the ball). Cheating involves drawing an unseen token which may give you the cheating player extra strength or extra fans, or may disqualify him. The winner of each match is decided by the total strength of cards on each side, modified by cheating and possession of the ball.

BBTM is fun if played at a reasonably fast pace. It's not so fun if players are spending too much time analyzing your options. This is a light, chaotic, theme-heavy game. It works best when played as such. Even when played at the proper pace, I feel like the game lasts one round too long if you have the full complement of four players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blood Bowl Team Manager is a 2 to 4 player card game.  The goal of the game is to get the most fans after the 5 (4 in a 2 player game) season.  During a season, each manager compete at (generally) 2 highlight at the time.  At each turn, you place one of your team's player on one highlight.  Your objective is to beat the opposing coach at the other end of the field.  The team that have the most Star Power on his side of the field wins the highlight and take the central payout in addition to his side of the field payout.  If the payout is not more fan, it will help you for the next seasons.  You can gain star players, team upgrade or staff upgrade.
Most of the player in your team have skills that can be use to take the ball, draw a card from your deck, tackle the opposing player or cheat.
Some season also have a tournament (with bigger payout) where all players can participate.
The winner is the player who has the more fan after the final season that ends with the Blood Bowl.

There is a lot of diversity in the game deppending on which team you're playing :
- Human are a well balance team.
- Dwarf are tough and well armourded.
- Wood elf  are good at controlling the ball.
- Skaven are fast (can draw more cards) and cheats.
- Orc are tough and tackle a lot.
- Chaos are cheaters and try to injured the opponents.

RATING: 7
D.A

Es un juego de cartas con algo de deckbuilding bastante competente. en el juego cada jugador lleva a un equipo de la blood bowl (el equivalente del football americano que existe en el universo de warhammer fantasy) y participa en varias competiciones con el objetivo de conseguir el mayor numero de triunfos (para los cuales no necesariamente se deben ganar todas las competiciones). 

Como ya digo, es competente, esta bien pensado, y es medianamente variado para la tematica que tiene. 

Es un juego que es facilmente obnubilable en una coleccion grande y quedarse sin ver mesa, pero ni mucho menos un mal juego. recompensa las oportunidades que se le dan. no es magnifico, pero es un buen juego. 

PD. desde mediados de 2016 (cuando FFG y GWS se "divorciaron") este juego al dejar de ser producido y publicado, se ganó fama de "buscado" y con ello de "valorado" en la compraventa. En otras palabras: que ahora se vende usado mas caro que cuando se compraba nuevo, y se valora mejor ahora que cuando se fabricaba y vendia. Jolleros powah. Es un juego de 7 y de comprar a 30 pavitos si te pilla cerca y te cae simpatica la propuesta, no es un must have de 9 para comprar a 50+ expansiones aparte. La gente esta muy loca.

RATING: 6.5
Captures the Ameritrash, confrontational, chaotic, fiddly, luck-induced rage of Blood Bowl perfectly. I mean this in the best ways, but also as a caveat to those who don't like these type of games in general.

The game is area control, with a hint of asymmetrical play and mild taste of deckbuilding. There are 4-5 areas each turn you are trying to "win" in order to gain Fans (VP's), upgrade cards, or additional player cards for your deck. 

The famed (tackle/whiff/digger) Blood Bowl dice are here, for those of you keeping score.

In our group's sessions this game overstays its welcome slightly. The more players, the longer it gets - I worry about future expansions that may increase the number of players. 

Running time exponentially increases due to the game's fiddliness and an increasing abundance of staff and team upgrades each round, so even though it's "only" five matches, you'll be at the table at least 60 minutes, and the last match is a decathlon of checking a dozen cards for effects before, during, and after each action or die roll. Scoring gets more and more fiddly with each match as well. 

AP-prone players may not be your favorites if you play this with them. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Great card game with variable player powers.  It abstracts the on the field play of the miniatures game so that you can play a whole season .  This allows a deck building mechanic, as your team upgrades from match to match.  

Combines pretty good tactical card play with a little bit of hand management and deck building.  Its really an area majority style game where your units are cards.  The game is as much about timing and card placement as it is what your cards are.  

If you are a fan of blood bowl you will love the theming.  Even if you aren't a fan, the game incorporates enough generic football terminology to make it more than just an abstract area majority card game.

Of course with six factions and a slew of upgrade cards the replayability is excellent.   

My only real complaints about the game are that it is a little long (probably solved with more experience and familiarity) and some of the victory point granting upgrade cards are strong enough to require everyone at the table to take note of them and actively try to stop players who are going that route.  I played twice and both games were dominated by those cards.  I still think its a great design.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
When I first heard about this game, I was intrigued. I've always liked the theme of Blood Bowl and I am big fan of Battleball. Mainly due to cost of entry, I've never played Blood Bowl, so I hoped this might scratch the same itch. Well it doesn't, but I don't think it's supposed to.

The concept of managing a team instead of actually controlling the players doing the skull-cracking sounds a bit boring by comparison. However, there is a bit more battling in here than you might think at first. The best thing mechanically about this game is the ball. Basically, battles take place by each player committing cards with various strengths to each battle. Add up the numbers, highest number wins. Simple, but boring. However, the ball really takes this up a notch. Each battle has a ball that the cards can fight over. It not only serves as two bonus points towards winning the battle, it also is a tiebreaker. Many of the special abilities on the cards revolve around taking the ball, forcing fumbles, etc. and this works very nicely.

However, I was somewhat disappointed by the lack of variety in the teams. Sure, they have different special abilities that give them a different feel, but their stats are almost all the same. Fully a third of the cards are EXACTLY the same across all teams, and there is some duplication beyond this. I think balance could have been maintained while still creating a bit more variety.

There is a minor deckbuilding element as well, which basically amounts to getting to add a random extra-good card to your deck a couple times a game. These "star player" cards are quite useful and have some special abilities not seen on any of the cards in the basic decks. I wish these would have been better integrated into the game, as they add a lot of interest to an otherwise samey game.

All in all, it's a nice effort, a good price, and some really well-written rules (no easy task in a game where players/players/plays/playing all mean different things). I just feel like it's a pretty fun game that could have been a REALLY fun game if they weren't striving so much for balance. Too much of that makes it sometimes feel like a game of adding numbers instead of a game of "kill-the-guy-with-the-ball".

RATING: 4
Blood Bowl: Team Manager is a multi-player, multi-location tug-of-war with a lot of special power sauce slathered all over it. With that in mind, I imagine that this is best played quick, dirty, with a pint in hand, and with a sailor's mouth. While that's not how my first play went down (i.e., it was 210 minutes, over-analyzed, and in a space in which no one was too foul of mouth), I can see the potential here. I say potential because this game potentially suffers from over-analysis -- there is *so* much differing text on the cards: this is the bane of players who need to know (or the bane of players who don't like waiting for the player who "needs to know"). However, with the right group playing fast, furious, and on the edge of their seat, this could be a lot of fun. Otherwise, it becomes bogged down by its own textual weight (which makes the game feel "heavier" than its otherwise simple structure conveys).

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
“Klytus! Are your men on the right pills? Maybe you should execute their trainer!” -Emperor Ming

GAMEPLAY
A game is broken into five rounds of highlights. Each round lets players vie for the rewards from more star players to coaching abilities to fans. Players commit a player from their hand of six to a highlight in an attempt to pick up the ball or knock down other players. Play moves smoothly through the rounds as star players enter the match and upgrades become a big influence. Upgrades range from a mercenary wizard to blast an opponent to extra training to knock someone out to rewards of fans for hurting a player. This ia a fairly strategic game with luck involved in the player deck shuffle, cheating tokens, and the dice roles for tackling opponents. The winner is the player with the most fans at the end of the fifth round.
COMPONENTS
Cards are very well designed with bright colorful and stylized art. The art is spot on blood bowl, unhinged fantasy. The card is good quality and the tokens are all thick stock. The style is spot on Blood Bowl and if you know the world you will love it.
THEME
If you enjoy blood bowl the miniatures game you will enjoy this game. Committing players to highlights is a little abstract, it doesn’t really feel like individual games played each round. There is a good struggle for control of highlights as your more powerful players get mixed in towards the later rounds.
WHO IS IT FOR?
This game should be enjoyed over a beer. It can be learned by younger players but the raucous nature of Blood Bowl is great for a casual play through with some cursing. Playing with 3 or 4 players allows everyone to win some highlights and keep the game interesting.

RATING: 7.5
Trying to evolve a miniatures board game into a cards game is something very difficult to do, specially if you want to emulate the game as the original was. In this case, the designers didn't try to copy that but, instead, they created a new concept using as a base the original Blood Bowl. In the team manager version, what you do is compete against other players in different games every turn, and what is being represented is the highlight of the game: that play where the blitzer killed the quarterback or when the quarterback made the perfect pass through a bunch of rivals... that kind of stuff. I think that the idea is very interesting and, in fact, it works very well.
However, I do think that this game needs the expansions. The game improves a lot. The expansions, as far as I know, and at least in Spain, are out of stock. I do not know if they are going to be reprinted, which is a problem as I only own the core box.
Positive:
1. The theme is well implemented
2. Easy to explain
3. Great artwork
Negative:
1. Better with the expansions (which are out of stock, in Spain at least)
2. There are some number of players that do not work very well because of the amount of games available
3. It may be a bit long
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

I think at the end of the day, I would probably choose BL over this even though there is some added fun/neat aspects to it and it scales 2 to 4, I should play it again though but really I now have a boatload of card games this has to compete with.

The game is very well done actually, and the theme is pretty strong, also liked it a little more with 2, though I could see how playing with 4 as two teams might be the most fun, but overall I just don't think the game is for me as too much relies on luck and is almost fully tactical.

RATING: 7
Fun card game played in a series of rounds. In each round each player has hand of six cards which are played alternately against one of three 'prize' cards in the middle of the table with the highest total against each prize taking that prize in a similar manner to a number of Knizia card games.

A number of twists keep it interesting, including a blizzard of special effects, a variety of creature decks with varying pros and cons, the ability to improve your deck and a tussle over holding the ball counter on the prize cards which adds two points to your score against that card if held at the end of the round.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
IN BBTM, you play out 5 "weeks" of games. Highlight and tournament cards become the fields of play and define rewards for each match up. Players play to either side of the highlights and tournament cards. In a 4-player game, players each compete on two of four highlight match ups. All four teams can play to a tournament. You draw a hand of six cards and on your turn you either pick a new matchup or strengthen a position you already have. Player cards have a "Star Power" as well as defined abilities and skills. All are executed when the card is played. Players also may have support cards they earned in previous rounds that they can play to help. If you win a match up, rewards are defined on the card. It can be additional fans, team upgrades, star players, and so on. This leads to good variety from one round to the next as new things come into play.

It's not a complicated or "thinky" game, by any means. It is a romp going head-to-head with the other asymmetrical races and teams. Your race and card abilities give you clues as to how to play them and creates a lot of great atmosphere. You are trying to gain more fans, not necessarily win games. It helps top win, but fans can be acquired in many ways. This is a well-designed game of stupid fun that I'll play any time!

RATING: 8.5
Kind of a take-that card game that involves a small amount of drafting/deck building, all themed around a bloody football game played by different fantasy races.
On paper, it didn't seem the kind of game I'd particularly be into. But in actually playing it, I loved it. It reminded me a bit of Chaos Marauders, although I liked this one better. I really got into the theme, and they went all out here, with awesome awesome art, tons of flavor text and theme-related mechanisms. It's got your typical FFG chrome-heavy rules, so you need someone to know the rules well, especially as you get late in the game and have a lot of card interactions. Don't try to play this out of the box. One of the cool things is each team has its own strengths and weaknesses, thematic to its race (orcs, chaos demons, humans, elves, etc), with its own customized team upgrade deck.

RATING: 7

RATING: 8.5
I love this game!  Death Sport board games are very, very appealing to me & this game fits the bill beautifully.  The only reason I give it a rating of "8.5" is due to the fact there aren't enough teams to choose from, extra Highlight cards & Headline & Tournament cards in the "Spike! Magazine" deck.  But, with that said, this IS FF Games so I'm sure the expansion sets are lining up for release as I write this.  The concept is fantastic--managing a team within the BB League, with emphasis not only on Team Match-Ups, but Staff upgrades & drafting Star Players as well.  This brings so much more to the BB League world through card-play, deck-building & dice chucking.  The goal is not how many Match-ups you win, but how man FANS your team acquires over a 5 week season.  Again, this makes the game so cool & with the death sport theme, even cooler!  If you are already a BB fan (or a fan of Elfball, GavBall or DreadBall), then you must pick up this game.  When I get the SUDDEN DEATH expansion, I'm sure this game will rise to a rating of "9" or "10".

RATING: 7.5
This is a card game based on the Bloodbowl universe. Surprisingly deeper and more tactical than I first assumed. There's a lot to consider. Broken down to bare mechanics, I would say that essentially this is a bidding game. Player bid "footballers" of various strengths to win prizes, which can be taken as Fan Factor (VPs) or new tactics or new players.

Its quite exciting and tense, but personally ran a bit too long for me. Towards the end game, everyone had so many cards in front of them that it was hard to track who had which powers. I'd prefer a quicker, less cluttered game.

RATING: 8
LIKES:

* Really enjoyable deckbuilding game of a sort where you fight in a couple matches for different rewards.  
* Victory in a match were variable and you could go for strategy cards, star players, or points.
* Each player deck has certain tendencies which are unique to the race.
* The different athlete cards have differing abilities which can effect a match in very different ways.  
* This game has lots of expansion possibilities.  
* Dice are involved in a pretty solid way where you play the percentages if you choose to tackle, etc...
* "Cheating is required" - you have to like a game where this in typed in the instructions...:-)  Of course, cheating is a specific mechanic involved with the "evil" races and can be both good or bad.

DISLIKE:

* Some of the strategy cards seem a bit overpowered compared to others.  
* Game may overstay its welcome by around 30 minutes...particularly on your first play or two as you figure out the text on the cards and/or have AP players involved.

RATING: 8
[u]Comments:[/u]
Now this little gem is a tight card game where the whole is much larger than the just the sum of its parts. At its heart Blood Bowl is a simple area majority game where each area is competed over in a number of rounds (usually four or five). Games can move very quickly, especially with players who know what they are doing. The opportunity to make your team what you want it to based on your winning (and even just competing) in some competitions offer a variety to the game. Each team has its own strengths and weaknesses that the player will do well to heed during a game (both yours and your opponents). The components are all high quality (per usual with FFG) and the graphic layout of the components are also well done. Overall the game hums along at a really nice brisk pace, and has a ton of interesting choices to make and a nice dash of randomness that will make every matchup thrilling. Definitely looking forward to trying the expansions as well.

RATING: 6
* Components
+ Very good components
+ The tokens were very easy to punch out
- The card drawings are a little dark
$ The cards seem good enough.  I prefer a linen finish to their glossy finish, as it feels like it makes for more robust cards, but these are fine.
+ The insert has the right size.

* After a first game:

I found the game to be quite light, with not so many difficult decisions; much lighter than Schotten-Totten, Memoire 44 (where to move which troops is often not obvious), Claustrophobia (choosing where to go, whether to split the group or not, how to use the dice, etc. require some thoughts),….  However, we did not play optimally, as we forgot to use our Upgrades (Team or Staff), so there *is* something to learn (I look forward to this).

The game was entertaining enough, but felt really too light to be very interesting, for me.  Maybe it could become more interesting if I paid more attention to the distribution of players (which players were played, which are to come).  I should also try to better use the special abilities (including taking into account my opponent's).

RATING: 8
Fútbol americano táctico,azaroso,tramposo y divertido protagonizado por las razas más conocidas del mundo Warhammer: elfos, enanos, orcos, skaven, caos y humanos; 6 razas distintas con diferentes formas de entender y practicar este deporte. Esto es lo que vas a encontrar en este juego en el que cada jugador representa a un entrenador de un equipo de indeseables y facinerosos con un único objetivo: ser el mejor en su profesión gracias al atraer el mayor número de hinchas posible a su equipo.
Un juego más profundo de lo que parece en un principio y con más factor suerte del que uno desearía, pero un buen juego, sesudo y divertido al tiempo, del que sin duda no tardarán en aparecen expansiones con más razas disponibles; expansiones que por otra parte este humilde jugador comprará debido a la buena impresión que el juego le ha causado.

Digo táctico porque cada equipo tiene sus puntos fuertes y débiles y la pericia del jugador consiste en sacar el mayor beneficio de los primeros y el menor perjuicio de los segundos, utilizando en el momento más adecuado tal o cual carta de jugador y sabiendo elegir con tiento qué tipo de "momentos estelares" se ajusta más a las necesidades de su equipo y de la situación en la que se encuentra en cada momento.

Nota 1: Hay diferencias entre ser ó no el jugador inicial de una ronda; según qué razas son más productivas cuando van a rebufo y menos cuando deben llevar la iniciativa; por eso, el jugador debe elegir un tipo de "momentos estelares" con mayores hinchas en la parte central de estas cartas cuando tiene mayores posibilidades de victoria y debe elegir otros "momentos estelares" más conservadores cuando se encuentre en una situación en la que el orden de los turnos le desfavorezca.
También debe tener en cuenta a la hora de seleccionar los "momentos estelares" qué tipos de recompensa de zona debe elegir; unas zonas que compensen los puntos débiles del equipo sería lo ideal, ya que aunque se pierda la recompensa central la de zona siempre se tiene mientras el jugador tenga al menos un personaje en ese momento estelar.
Está claro también que si un jugador tiene amplia ventaja en hinchas respecto a sus rivales, una buena estrategia puede ser elegir momentos estelares donde las recompensas no sean grandes cantidades de hinchas; de esta manera mantiene su ventaja mientras opta a reforzar su equipo para próximas rondas.
Por otro lado, un equipo que va atrás en el marcador necesita todo lo contrario; elegir momentos estelares en los que las recompensas sean de hinchas; así podrá recortar distancias con respecto a sus rivales.
Nota 2:¡IMPORTANTE! Repito, el orden del turno de jugadores es vital, ya que algunas razas funcionan mejor cuando deben defender una posición que cuando deben atacarla. Por eso es importante conocer las limitaciones y ventajas de cada raza.

Digo azaroso porque el azar está muy presente. Por un lado en el lanzamiento de dados y por otro en las fichas de trampa.
En cada uno de los dos dados hay un 50% de posibilidades de que un placaje tenga éxito, luego mala pata aparte es un factor que favorece bastante a las razas con alto potencial ofensivo si no durante toda la partida sí al menos al principio (las 2 primeras rondas), lo que por otro lado puede ser suficiente si en esas 2 rondas esos equipos han obtenido suficiente ventaja; en las siguientes rondas deben preocuparse de mantener esa distancia.
Las fichas de trampa son 30 y de ellas sólo 6 son negativas (20%), ya que suponen la expulsión de un jugador de un enfrentamiento; 4 son inocuas y 20 positivas. Una bendición más que una maldición que de nuevo favorece a las razas ofensivas que suelen ser las que más fichas de trampas roban durante el juego.
Para minimizar un poco el factor de las fichas de trampa lo que he decidido ha sido lo siguiente: una ficha de trampa que ha sido usada no se devuelve a la pila de reserva al inicio de la siguiente ronda, sino que se aparta; de esta manera aumentan las posibilidades de que salgan las fichas de expulsión a medida que avanza la partida y se van robando más fichas de trampas; y parece lógico pensar que a más trampas haga un equipo más posibilidades tiene de que el árbitro les pille in fraganti cometiendo alguna pillería. En el caso hipotético de que se hubieran usado todas las fichas de trampa antes de terminar la partida lo que hay que hacer es barajarlas todas de nuevo y formar una nueva reserva.

Nota 3: Está claro que a más cartas de mejora de equipo y de cuadro técnico y jugadores estrella tenga un equipo más posibilidades tendrá de obtener una victoria, por lo que debe ser algo a tener presente en la elección de los momentos estelares, pero siempre teniendo en cuenta que deben servir además para compensar las carencias que tengan un equipo o bien reforzar alguna de sus virtudes.
Algunas razas necesitan de forma más imperiosa que otras algunas de estas 3 características; intentaré reflejarlo en mi análisis de las razas.

RAZAS

Caos:
Raza ofensiva y equilibrada ya que en una misma carta de jugador tienen tanto habilidades de placaje, pase y trampa; por lo tanto pueden hacer un placaje al rival, hacer que este caiga derribado reduciendo sus puntos de estrellato y soltando el balón, que luego pueden coger con su habilidad de pase. El único inconveniente es que roban muchas fichas de trampa y pueden resultar expulsados, pero ya hemos visto que tampoco es algo demasiado negativo.
Es una raza que funciona bien tanto si es la primera del turno en entrar en acción (tienen la habilidad de pase que les otorga la posesión del balón) como si van por detrás (te placan y te roban el balón).
Es probable que ganen la primera ronda del juego, en la que deberían optar por momentos estelares que les otorgaran el mayor número posible de hinchas para tener un cojín con respecto a sus rivales, pero seleccionando zonas de juego propias que además les otorguen mejoras de equipo y cuadro técnico que siempre son necesarias.
Creo que deberían optar por los jugadores estrella y las mejoras de cuadro técnico.

Elfos:
Equipo limpio que no hace trampas, lo que es más un inconveniente que ventaja. El equipo está desequilibrado ya que algunos jugadores únicamente hacen placaje y otros únicamente realizan pases de balón, pero no ambas cosas en la misma carta, luego pueden hacer un placaje al rival pero como mucho devuelven el balón al centro del campo (pero no a sus manos) y si consiguen el balón mantienen de pie a los rivales con todos sus puntos de estrellato, lo que hace que los rivales lo tengan más fácil a la hora de ganar los torneos y momentos estelares.
No es un equipo que funcione bien cuando es el primero en actuar; debe reservar sus jugadores de placaje para el final si no quiere desperdiciar esa habilidad, por lo que se ve obligado a utilizar a sus jugadores de pase en primer momento. De esta forma los rivales podrán placarles fácilmente y robarles el balón. Posteriormente los elfos podrán utilizar sus jugadores de placaje pero ya no podrán recuperar la posesión del balón y esos valiosos +2 a los puntos de estrellato que otorga. En estos turnos es perferible que los elfos estén preparados para perder sus rondas y elijan momentos estelares con zonas centrales que no otorguen demasiados hinchas pero que tengan zonas de juego propias que sí los otorguen para así ganar algún hincha; tampoco viene nunca mal una zona de juego propia que otorgue jugadores estrella, ya que éstos son especialmente importantes para esta raza ya que pueden compensar el desequilibrio que padecen.
Los turnos en los que van por detrás los elfos funcionan mejor, ya que en un primer momento pueden intentar un placaje y antes de terminar la ronda pueden intentar robar el balón al rival y ganar la bonificación de +2 de cara a la fase de marcador y así intentar asegurarse la victoria. En estos turnos es cuando los Elfos deben intentar conseguir más hinchas en torneos y momentos estelares.
Sus mejoras deben ser jugadores estrella y cartas de mejoras de ambos tipos.

Skaven:
Son una versión más débil pero más rápida de los ejércitos del Caos, ya que son menos tramposos y menos ofensivos. Aunque tienen personajes que hacen placajes no suelen tener la habilidad de pase; las habilidades de pase están concentradas en otras cartas que tienen 2 pases seguidos y que además tienen la habilidad de "Esquivar" que hacen repetir el lanzamiento de dados de un rival que les intente placar.
Son parecidos a los elfos pero con habilidades de ataque mejores, luego al igual que éstos van bien en turnos en los que van por detrás pero no van del todo mal si juegan en primer lugar porque la habilidad esquivar les da una segunda oportunidad ante los ataques rivales.
Tienen buenas habilidades de equipo, que hay que potenciar en cuanto sea posible en las zonas de juego propias de los momento estelares. Los jugadores estrella también serán bien recibidos.

Enanos:
Apenas tienen personajes con la habilidad de pase,luego es poco probable que tengan el balón en sus manos; este factor queda compensado con la habilidad "Mantenerse firme" que evita que sus jugadores sean placados mientras sean portadores del balón. Por tanto, frente a equipos con pocos jugadores de pase puede ser el factor desequilibrante. El poder de estrellato de los enanos de placaje tampoco es demasiado elevado, luego tampoco son demasiado efectivos, pero... 
Tienen 1 ventaja: cuando son derribados el poder de estrellato tiene escasa merma, luego ofrecen una buena resistencia a la hora de dejar escapar torneos y momentos estelares. Debido a este hecho pueden arriesgarse a atacar a jugadores rivales que tengan poder de estrellato mayor que ellos. La habilidad "Defensa" de muchos de ellos potencia este aspecto.
Sus jugadores estrella tienen la habilidad de pase y sus mejoras de equipo son bastante buenas, luego son un equipo robusto difícil de vencer.

Orcos:
Equipo equilibrado que realiza trampas de forma moderada y buenos placajes, factor en el que destacan y que hay que potenciar con sus cartas de mejora de equipo. Aunque no tiene demasiados jugadores con pase (lo que puede suponer un problema frente a equipos que retengan el balón),los que tiene usan la habilidad "Manos seguras" que les hace resistentes a las pérdidas del balón. Aún así es muy recomendable conseguir cuanto antes jugadores estrella que remedien esta carencia.
Algunos jugadores además tienen habilidades que reportan hinchas al herir o derribar a sus rivales, aspecto que permite sumar buenos PV a lo largo de la partida.
Funcionan bien tanto si juegan en primer como en segundo lugar.

Humanos:
Su punto fuerte son los jugadores que al placar con éxito reciben la propiedad del balón.Esto compensa que sus jugadores de pase no son de los mejores del juego. El problema es que el valor de estrellato de esos jugadores es de 3, luego placar y quitar el balón a jugadores de valor 3 ó 4 de puntos de estrellato rivales se antoja algo difícil, por lo que dicha habilidad sólo es efectiva ante rivales no demasiado duros.
Es una raza que funciona mejor cuando va al rebufo y peor cuando tiene que tomar la iniciativa.
Sus mejoras de equipo priman la posesión del balón, luego son recomendables, pero lo son más la necesidad de obtener más jugadores estrella con mejores capacidades tanto físicas como de pase.

RATING: 9
Well, it's a little box, but the game is huge.

There is some luck factor involved, but it's not THAT much important. I'm myself a very unlucky dice roller (i know that statistically it shouldn't exist, but play a game against me and you'll start believing so!), but I NEVER lost a single game in BloodBowl, so strategy (a grand plan, usually crafted around the first upgrade cards you receive) and tactic (the instant decisions and analysis meant to let you choose the right card to play your guys on, or how to pass, which cards to combine to have a solid answer to the opponent's abilities...) comes into play heavily. 

The components are top quality, the teams are fun and feel really different, even if they aren't perfectly balanced, but it could really be a good way to help new players to start the game. 

Lenght is ok, don't expect to finish it in a couple of turns, but it won't waste all your night, either.

In the end, one of the best surprises I had in the boardgaming world.

A solid 9! (because I will give 10 only to the TOP game of my collection)

RATING: 8
It's an interesting variation of battle line mechanics.  Different players play their "troops" on different parts of the line, activating game effects when they do so that disable opponent's troops, move stuff around, or seize "the ball".  The ball is worth extra points, and some mechanics interact with the ball carrier.

The gameplay is a lot like Smash Up.

Seemingly unnecessarily fiddly and repetitious
Takes 90 to 120 minutes to play a game
Seems to have runaway leader and loser issues
Not convinced teams are well-balanced

Overall, I really want to like the game, but haven't enjoyed it due to runaway leader and length of play issues.  I'd rather play Innovation or Glory to Rome, if I want some euro-cardy-chaotic mechanics.

RATING: 7
With no prior Blood Bowl experience, I wasn't sure what to expect from this. I was pleasantly surprised: It's a meaty game (meatier than it looks from its slim little box) full of interesting decisions -- and chaos. Lots of chaos, die rolls, and gambles, but all implemented well in that you have an enjoyable amount of control over it.

As a big fan of the WFRP world, I love that every team's flavor comes out so clearly in its deck and play style. Based on one play, they all seem solid. Flavor across the board is good, too, especially the star players.

Surprise comebacks are entirely possible, the cheating is a hoot, and everything seems to scale well based on player count. Good stuff!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
In Blood Bowl: Team Manager - The Card Game players loosely take on the roll of general managers of fantasy inspired football teams.  The goal is to be the team that generates the most fans by the end of the game.  

Using a card drafting mechanic players will make their teams (read: hand of cards) better to increase their chance of victory over their opponents.  On a player's turn, they will play a card out to "highlight" cards in the middle of the table.  This is similar to playing cards to bases in Smashup. After players' hands are exhausted points will be counted up at each of the highlight cards.  The player with the most points wins the majority of benefits of that card.  There are also tournament cards which are similar to highlight cards, but give greater benefits.

Play goes on for five rounds.  The final round includes the "Blood Bowl".  Again, whomever has the most fans at the end wins.

Blood Bowl: Team Manager - The Card Game is silly fun.  It's neat to play your player cards up against your opponent's and see what happens.  There's usually a tug-of-war that happens over a football at each highlight card that you are squared off over.  Having said that I didn't feel like I was compelled to play it again soon.  It's a nice game to bring out every so often.

RATING: 9
Ihr wollt Eure Mitspieler mal so richtig ärgern und nerven?! Konfrontation ist Euer Ding?! Ihr gebt einenDreck auf kooperative Spiele?!
Dann solltet Ihr unbedingt einmal Blood Bowl: Team Manager spielen!
Das Stand-alone Kartenspiel bedient sich natürlich dem Szenario von Warhammer Fantasy, in dem Mannschafften von Menschen, Zwergen und Orks in einer blutigen Football-Variante aufeinander treffen. Jeder Spieler sieht sich zu Beginn des Spiels ein Team aus. In unterschiedlichen Matches, müssen nun die eigenen Spieler geschickt eingesetzt werden, um möglichst viele Belohnungen zu bekommen. Zusätzliche "Star"-Spieler werten den eigenen Spielerkader auf, ebenso Team- und Personalverbesserungen. So entsteht ein verbissener Kampf, bei dem sich die Spieler nichts gönnen. Am Ende gewinnt der Spieler, dessen Mannschaft die meisten Fans sammeln konnte. Blood Bowl ist knallhart, taktisch tiefsinnig und einfach nur "Voll auf die Omme" ! Ich liebe es :-)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
One of only a few card driven games I've thoroughly enjoyed enough to want to come back to again and again!

Yes I'm already a big fan of the Blood Bowl miniatures game, but in fairness this could have been a reason for hating it just as much as it could have been for liking it (as I'm technically the harder fan to please)!

I'm reminded of FFG's Space Hulk Deathwing card game but with deeper, more strategic rules- players play against each other to score the most points for different rewards. Fans (victory points) are most important, but getting star players, special coaching and training cards can also help towards assuring victory.

Quite light with both an acceptable level of randomness and good chance for strategy, combined with a theme that captures the essence of Blood Bowl very well without leaving the uninitiated out of the loop.

Can go on just a little too long for what it is (some of our games have stretched to the 3 hour mark), but nobody really seems to notice it which is a good sign!

Surprising balance between the different teams for FFG too.

The available expansions bring a plethora of additional teams and lots of extra rules to make the game more chaotic and fiddly. I'm not sure all things are necessary, but it's at least fun to have the extra team options.

At first I thought the expansion teams' extra rules and abilities would make them more powerful, but repeated plays has seen them beaten by the vanilla teams on more then one occasion so balance seems to be ok for the moment.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Theme: Blood Bowl

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This one catches the feel of the actual board and miniatures version Blood Bowl surprisingly well. 

There are six teams to choose from, and they play differently enough to add variety. Elves are fast and control the ball, Orcs hit hard and cheat, and so on.
There might be some balancing issues though. Might…

A team consists of 12 players, represented by a card each. Coaches send their players to Match-ups, representing highlights from matches. The team with the most powerful players wins the match-up. However, players have different skills and abilities that spices things up.

This seems rather straightforward, but choosing what player to use at what moment is surprisingly difficult.

Winning a match-up allows coaches to upgrade their teams with star players and different team abilities. And, obviously, get Fans. The team with the most fans wins the game.

Playtime might be a bit on the long side. Apart from that, I really like Team Manager.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game requires the right... kind of player.  Mainly, someone with the heart of a 12-year-old boy, willing to throw elbows and play dirty in order for his "fantasy football" team to win the playoffs.  It reminds me of the soccer manager computer games that were popular in the '90s with a better sense of humor.  And yet, it requires more than a bit of forethought regarding how you're going to play your hand, which matches are worth going into, knowing when to count your losses, and above all else understanding your team and what it needs for victory.

I'd be ranking this one an 8 if the full spectrum of Blood Bowl teams was represented.  But they didn't, and since it's Fantasy Flight you can prepare yourself for the inevitable onslaught of overpriced expansion packs...

2017 UPDATE: Well, two inevitable updates later, and yes... it's an 8 now.  IF you buy the expansions.  The 6.75 rating on its own remains.  Also, I didn't realize the soccer sims were still a thing -- Football Manager 14 is my new single-player Through the Ages.

RATING: 5.5
It's an area control confrontation game with a bit of deck building that reminded me of the recent [thing=158435]Dog of War[/thing]. Blood Bowl is more random, and much more thematic. They have done a great job recreating the real Blood Bowl game experience, and the components are not lavish, but they are top quality, with great illustrations. My biggest complain in this regard is the difficulty to distinguish the cards of some of the teams.

Besides the strong theme integration, the different teams being quite asymetric is the strongest positive feature.

It is a very random game:
-> The luck of the draw.
-> You compete against several players at the same time, if both of them focus their biggest effort agains you, you will fall behind.
-> The reward cards are quite unbalanced, and so are the Star players.
-> The random cheat tokens.
-> The dice rolls.

It would be a great game for me if it was much shorter, but being on the verge of 2 hours, it's definitly too long for such a random game.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Pretty sweet little next-gen deckbuilder. Plays like Knizia's Battle Line on crack: players compete to win matchups by playing their dudes on one side or the other of a card that offers various awards. You always get "something" for playing, and something better for winning. Six races, lots of variation in style between them. You can end up with a big tableau of ongoing bennies/boosts on your side, which I found to be a headache to manage (9 cards at the end of a game where I was playing da Orks). 

I worry there's a bit of swinginess in final scoring, and maybe scoring in general. One player pulled a...can't remember, some kind of team upgrade card...that gave him 7 points on the final turn, thereby granting him a win purely on the luck of the draw. Did not love that.

I'd put this one about on-par with Rune Age, as a really sweet, thinky filler.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Schotten-Totten meets Taj Mahal with slatherings of luck. There's 4 matchup cards to be fought over in the middle (and sometimes a fifth) with a reward just for surviving there and bigger rewards if you have more star power there than the opponent who's committed to the other side of that matchup card. There's the Schotten-Totten. Here though, when you play, you usually get to roll so see if you can injure (lessen the star-power) or kill off an opponent's card. There's some luck. Lots of other cards get a random chit, which could be more star-power or VPs or might kill you off. Which means unless you over-commit, who wins is going to be a lottery. The Taj Mahal aspect is that if two of you go all out over 1 matchup card, the other two players are going to clean up over the other 3 (or 4) matchup cards, so don't start a land war in Asia. Anyway, rewards are VPs or better cards or special power cards. Repeat for 5 rounds, most VPs wins. The game is about to trying to manage the chaos as best you can, making best use of the card effects you have to hand, and accepting the luck if you want to enjoy the game. And hope you don't get sucked into too many Asian land wars. There ain't a lot of finesse involved, with the main decision being what fights you want to pick and how much you listen to the whining whinging about who to pick on and who's winning. It's thematically fun but probably runs too long for what it gives back.

RATING: 7
Medium weight deck building/base scoring game with a fantasy American football theme (orcs, elves etc.).  Uses a competitive card play mechanic where cards are played at 'matches' with the highest overall score being the winner.  Also has some deck building mechanics where better players and tactics can be added to the basic starting team as a reward for winning matches.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Yes, this is a deckbuilding game, but the emphasis on deckbuilding is very small--you only add a couple of cards to your deck (and they're random), and you probably won't see them more than twice.  The real action here is the tactical play of cards to various "highlights", where you're competing with a single opponent for numerical supremacy.  The "cheating" tokens added a random element.  This game was definitely more tactical than anything else, and did elicit the head-to-head feel of football.  Point swings due to randomly drawing end-game scoring cards was a bit much.

RATING: 8
This game was suggested by friends and I thoroughly enjoy playing it. It is definitely more fun with more players. It is a really good balance between ease of play with some random elements combined with some solid strategy.

It reminds me a lot of Warhammer; in that you can do your best to put your troops/players into the right situations and hope you get average dice rolls. Some games you get some really bad luck, but at that point you can just play a spoiling game and try and take down the leading player or try some wacky strategy to try and fluke a win.

I have overdosed on this game a bit but am always willing to play. I feel the balance is pretty solid. I have both expansions and feel they are definitely worth the purchase.

RATING: 7

RATING: 7
As a long time Blood Bowl player, I was quite pleased to get to pick this up very cheaply 2nd hand at a convention. Finally got to give it a try at the weekend at Gaelcon

The game is relatively simple to understand, but definitely helps when you have someone to explain it. With up to 5 matches to fight over, which game you choose to participate in can be a big decision. Do you join in for the one with bigger prizes, or go for the lower prize that others will not likely compete against you for?

The game gets pretty chaotic and all the different races seemed pretty balanced to me. I thought it was a pretty fun game and glad I was able to pick it up at a very nice price!

RATING: 7
This game should not work or be fun.

It has lots of ridiculous tacked on theme that emerged quite well with the straight-forward and somewhat subtle area control maneuvering.  It has lots of explicit randomness that averages out reasonably well and allows for plenty of mitigation and reactions.  It has lots of leader bashing politics, mitigated with enough tactical efficiency variation to make for interesting choices and informed alliances.  The asymmetric factions have rock-paper-scissors relations that may only be balanced in multi-player matches, but which are close enough to still create tensions in an individual match.

With 2, a little luck can cause an early lead that ruins the run.  But it's still solid and pretty quick.
With 4+, the politics can overwhelm the game and suck up huge amounts of time, making the game overstay its welcome (but not be wholly unsatisfying).
With 3, it's great.  Play with exactly 3.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I expected deckbuilding gimmick du jour, but this was more like Chaos in the Old World: The Card Game. Asymmetric cards, upgrades, play your cards ('figures') into one of the highlights ('regions'), count majorities. Deck management is minimal, amounting to the incremental "place on top of draw deck' and 'only go through your deck ~5 times' seen in Mage Knight Board Game.

Spoiler alert: I've never encountered a '____: The Card Game" or "____ Express" that worked. Once you've tried the good stuff, you can't go back, even if playtime is halved.

Sports games now seem to go in 2 directions: actual simulation of the ball game using a ball marker and dice; or 'bracketology' games that cater to the fantasy side. BB:TM goes for the latter, in the vein of [thing=23604][/thing]. Having the ability to play anywhere (not even on your side) and managing multiple teams in the latter was more interesting though. In BB:TM, you contest a maximum of 2 highlights each round, plus the tournament if any (very rare to be able to jump into a 3rd highlight), and any time you win more than 1 highlight is a gift.

Fun as a quick filler and this rating might grow. Some areas of improvement:

The team upgrades don't seem to provide enough replayability, since you can end up decking it out. I'd rather it be CitOW-style choose-your-upgrade (for decision complexity), or have so many random team upgrades that it takes many plays to get through all the combinations (for card/rule complexity). This is probably the smallest quibble (just nitpicking here).

Drafting generic star players from the OWA and CWA decks isn't very exciting. These need to BREAK the game. And my opponents. Give me a MONSTER player deck here.

The players need to be more alive. Most just have "when enter play" abilities, and the rest have defensive abilities. More ways to manipulate and use the already-there players, including the downed ones, and move cheating tokens around would make it more dynamic. Maybe it's coming with an expansion (seemed like it with some cards referencing redundant situations), or it's in the Human, Wood Elf or Orc decks, which I haven't seen.

Lastly, this game needs to replace 'tackle' with JUMP/MUG, 'down' with INJURE/MAIM and 'injure' with KILL/CURB STOMP/POWER KICK IN THE NUTS/SKULL-CRUSHING FINALE. Why so PC?

CitOW references: 'Changer of Plays'

Base: 3+3
 + Sudden Death: 3+4

RATING: 6
[2013-10-27]
Amerikai foci kicsit brutálisan. A játékosok csapatok vezetői, akik hetente különböző meccseken vehetnek részt ezzel a rajongóik számát növelve, ami a játék célja. Ezen kívül egy-egy meccs sztárjátékosok felvételét, különböző csapatsegítő emberek, illetve saját fejlesztések elérését teszik lehetővé. Tehát van a játéknak egy pakliépítős része, hogy minél jobb játékosokból álljon a csapatunk, de itt is azt tudom mondani, hogy még pont követhető ez a paklifejlődés, mint a Mage Knightban és nem csak erről szól a játék. Van egy kombózási része is, a különböző segítők és saját fejlesztéslapjaink jó megválasztása tekintetében. Illetve van egy lapmenedzselő része is, hogy a körünkben felhasználható 6 lapunkat hogyan osszuk el az egyes meccsekhez. Jól kitalált a labda szerepe a játékban, jók az egyes játékosok képességei és érdekes módon elég jól megoldott a 3 és 4 játékos mód is, bár természetesen ez alapvetően egy 2 személyes játék. Összességében azt tudom mondani, nagyon kellemes meglepetés volt a Vérfoci. Nem túl bonyolult, mégis bőven van döntési helyzet a játékban. Negatívumként a lapok erősségének nem teljes kiegyenlítettségét tudom felhozni, illetve az egyes csapatokat sem éreztem igazán kiegyenlítettnek, de kétszemélyes játékban talán jobb ez is. Kicsit talán sok a lap, a saját fejlesztések mondjuk nem kellenének bele és jobban követhető lenne a végjáték is, illetve rajongókat sem adnék csak mondjuk meccsekkel, hogy ne legyen túl nagy szórás a végpontokban. Szóval, aki szereti a lapmendzselős játékokat és a komoly konfrontációt annak bátran ajánlom kipróbálásra.

RATING: 8
If you're a Blood Bowl fan and don't mind the fact that this game is all down to the random card draws then it could be the game for you and your Blood Bowl loving friends to sit down and have some fun with. However, if you like thing a little bit more cerebral, and want a game that is down to skill then look elsewhere. I've enjoyed playing the game and I think it's a worthy addition to my collection. but I'm not going to kid myself into thinking its some great strategic endeavour.

Gameplay 7.5 out of 10

RATING: 7
[i]Funny and Exciting Game Full of Drama. The Only Downside is the Abilities (they Get Fiddly) and Can Run Long![/i]

This is a pretty exciting game. It's always been fun every time I've played it! Cheating, tackling, it's all a lot of fun that can't really be had anywhere else short of the real Blood Bowl game.

Each team seems to have a flavor. Something I always dig. But unfortunately I think the players could stand to be more differentiated. Many of them share abilities across teams, and having every faction start with several identical throwaway linebackers is just boring. Please don't put such intentionally crappy cards in the game, and especially not in such numbers and across teams -- makes the Freebooter ability basically "get rid of a linebacker", and makes card-drawing better in comparison to the other abilities I think

I wish this game had just a little more strategy and depth. For first half of the game I'm usually having too much fun to notice, but this one can go up to 90-120 minutes with 4 players.

4 player is particularly offensive, because the level of fiddliness and bookkeeping surpasses the similar-but-way-deeper Chaos in the Old World. Keeping track of all the rewards during scoreboard phase can be a little tedious

There is errata in the FAQ that suggests just getting rid of certain Staff Upgrade cards. This seems necessary, but doesn't indicate that the game was tested very deeply because it seems to be quite an obvious problem with many groups finding it very early into the game's life cycle

The Sudden Death expansion is golden. Every element of the expansion, from contract payouts to new teams to ESPECIALLY the enchanted balls, gives the game more variability and flavor, more tactical depth, and more excitement (there's more fighting over the ball on the field and more for "already live" players to do because of enchanted balls and downed abilities, and because of contract payouts you don't know how many fans you even really have until the end).

[b]I'd Rather Play:[/b] Chaos in the Old World (At 4+ players)

(2 Design + 4 Enjoyment) - Without expansion and without errata.

With expansion and errata: (3 Design + 4 Enjoyment)

RATING: 8
This game feels very much like Smash Up but deeper, more fun, and even takes less time to play.  So all-in-all, better in every way.

In this game each player represents a team manager in the world of Blood Bowl trying to accumulate the most fans.  This is done across 5 rounds where each round a certain number of headlines/tournaments is placed out on the board.  Players play their Blood Bowl player cards on these headlines/tournaments in an attempt to accumulate the most star power and get the rewards for that card.  The depth of the game comes from the abilities on all the different players and upgrades you can get and how best to use them and in what order.  And there is a lot of depth and strategy to this reasonably simple game.

Plus the whole game, even with new players and teaching it to them first, can finish in under an hour.  Even quicker with experienced players.

I've heard complaints about the 2-player variant of this game and honestly I don't think it plays that different at all.  There's less competition and I prefer it with 3 or 4 but it works well for players that mostly play duo also.

RATING: 8
A great microcosm of a Blood Bowl season in card game form that takes a fraction of the time to play.  Just like real Blood Bowl, the teams are horribly unbalanced and some will always win when pitted against others; that's where playing with 3-4 players to help mitigate this comes in.  An excellent game as long as at least 3 are playing.  With two, you have to ensure that either two bashy or two fast teams play; otherwise, the speedy team will always win.  Not very fun for the bashy player, but at least this is true to the original Blood Bowl.

The theme is a little whack; there seems to be a real disconnect between committing players to "highlights" and "tournaments" and the actual game of Blood Bowl.  How can a simple lineman win an entire game just by being present?  Granted, I understand that the game was probably purposely simplified to keep the complexity low, but it doesn't feel all that thematic because of it.  As long as you can get past this and see it more as a hand management exercise, it becomes a fun game.
