RATING: 5.5
Like Death Angel, surprisingly effective at creating atmosphere -- the matches, Schotten Totten-like card clashes with ball tokens that bounce between the two sides, do create the same excitement as a rowdy sporting event, with the tackle dice and cheating tokens generating equal cheers and groans.

My problems with the game are twofold and related. Luck has far too much influence, to the point where no outcome feels like the result of any skill or good play: if it's not a failed tackle, it's a referee's whistle for cheating or lucky draw from one of the grossly imbalanced card decks.

The fun atmosphere would be compensation enough if not for the fact that it goes far, far, far too long for a game with this level of randomness. Teaching games routinely go for two hours! With experienced, faster players and one of the short-game variants, I can see enjoying the game as a filler, but it's not worth that level of time commitment.

RATING: 7
Love the basic game mechanisms, but it seems like the game's balance is way off. There are a few star players and abilities that just put others to shame. Especially so with some of the end game scoring cards that can net you a TON of points.

RATING: 7
I often hear people say that this game is better than they expected.  I'm inclined to agree.  I didn't expect to enjoy this game as much as I did when I first heard of it.  I think it is that the game doesn't play like (North American) football, but the theme makes it feel a lot like football.

Each player is a manager/coach of a team.  Your team consists of your starting deck of players.  When you play cards, you are actually assigning your players to compete for a highlight or tournament.  The player card may also have abilities that help you win the highlight.  Highlights can only have two players competing for them which means that the third or fourth player (if any) cannot participate in that highlight.  There are enough highlights in each round to choose from, so you should be able to compete in at least one.  There may be a tournament in a round as well and any number of teams can participate for the prizes of that tournament.

The goal is to have the most fans at the end of the game.  Winning and participating in some highlights and tournaments will win fans.  There are also other abilities and situations where you can also win fans.  Highlights and tournaments also have other prizes for winners and participants in terms of better team abilities or adding better players to your team.

This game feels like you are managing and coaching a football team.  Each game represents a football season and each round represents a week in the football season.  There are 5 rounds in total before the game ends and everyone tallies the fans they have acquired throughout the season to determine the winner.

The game can drag on.  There is quite a bit of thought going towards playing a card on your turn and you only play one card per turn.  I do like the fact that there is so much thought in each play.  A game with 3 players can last over 3 hours and longer with 4 players.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
Really good cardgame. Has similarities with Battle Line and Field of Glory (you are fighting for certain locations called 'pitches). 

Best thing though is that it captures the atmosphere of the Blood Bowl universe really well, and introduces some very fun chaos and campaign-like effects.

Quite impressed that it managed to capture the Blood Bowl spirit so well, differing so much from the 'real' Blood Bowl as actual game.

Will play this more often!

[UPDATEjan 2014] Played this again with friends, we had a great time, enjoyed by all. Recommended for anyone interested in light-hearted fun. It is a tactical game, not much strategy, and turns flow fast so it keeps you going. With three it plays as good as with two (maybe even better). Great game all around.

RATING: 9
Fantastic deck building game. You play as the manager of a fantasy sports league. The rules are extremely simple--just throw your guys on one side of a match, and the player with the highest numbers win. But there are a ton of ways to mess with other players, get extra points, and cheat, which keeps this from being a predictable game.

Best played with people who won't care if their seemingly guaranteed win was just lost because of a dice roll or a randomly selected tile. The randomness never feels too harsh or unfair, though.

RATING: 9
I love it! This card game bring you the feeling of the competition for the classic boardgame, but in a totaly different way. The trasposition of the background is perfect. The random result is still present but not only in dice rolls. If you hate luck based games forget it, but don't miss this gem if you like Blood Bowl. It could be a great surprise!

After playing it with good house rules this game shines!
- Before starting the round each player should select his action in turn order until all action (not tournament) are selected by two different teams.
- Select secretly player card to be placed in one action at the same time, but deploy them in turn order (reduce the table position effect).
- Remove high score cards which changes drastictly the final score.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
The randomness of hiring Freebooters and Stars almost breaks this game (and can break some individual plays) but there is enough going on in other aspects to help it retain most of the fun of Blood Bowl, with less tactics and less strategy.

It really doesn't need to be a Blood Bowl game, as it has almost nothing in common outside of theme.

I think I'd always rather play regular Blood Bowl, but this is a decent alternative for 4 people or those who have less than 2 hours.

Update: the more I play this the more apparent it becomes how massively luck heavy this is. A few dice rolls go in your favour at the start of the game and you might get to recruit 3 star players. If your opponent has none, you're then at a massive advantage in round 2. Do well in round 2... snowball effect. Conversely, if you get a couple of useless Freebooters over a Star Player, you're screwed. Some of the power-ups are just better than others. All in all, this is a nice idea, done badly with my pet hate of tiny cards that people need to be aware of across a table.

Rating down from 6.8 to 5.5.

RATING: 8
The game is a lot of fun to play!  The Cheat Token aspect does lead a nice bit of randomness.  And I like that the Star Player deck is chosen from all the teams that make up each of the two factions.  Nice to combine races and abilities in a single team.

Theme is excellent, and does a good job of fitting into the Blood Bowl universe.

Components are well made.  Not sure why it was limited to a 4-player game, when there are 6 races included, other than to make for an expansion.  I'm sure there will be many race expansions, since the main Blood Bowl game contains over 20 races in its current rules.

For an update: This is a great game, especially with the right group.  This game is more of a Beer-n-Pretzel game than a deep-strategy think-fest, so plan accordingly with your gaming group.

RATING: 9
I like it. The somewhat-high luck factor, between the dice and the random cheat tokens, really fits well with the theme in this case. This game has a really interesting take on deckbuilding, much like Core Worlds, in that you'll likely only go through your deck a couple of times per game.

Update: Have played this quite a bit now and I still love it. To appreciate this game you have to accept that it is about trying to get the most points while managing the chaos, not about carrying out some long-term strategy. Because of the cheat tokens you can never be sure of a win, so you have to try to spread out in hopes of winning at least something.

[b]Player Count Verdict: 3+[/b]
With two players you lose the Spike deck, which adds variety to the game. It's not bad with two players, but 3-4 is better.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
First Impression:

A well produced game with a crazy theme: warhammer 40K rugby!

First of all, theme and humour oozes from this game, from it's artwork, text, abilities, categories... pretty much everything. This is a classy thematic game and should be well respected for that. The core mechanism is also pretty solid. Multiple rugby "games" (area control) with variable rewards combined with deck handling/building give players a plethora of choices during the game that really matter. Few thematic games can claim that skill is rewarded more than in this game. The game also excells in the typical fields of thematic games. It's highly replayable, with several teams that feel differently and an impossible amount of extra coaches, transactions and team skills that will make even the same team never play the same twice. It's also quite fun, with just the right amount of tactical take that (and no kingmaking!), luck and agony (cheating!). Finally it flows really well, as the players really have little to calculate and more to commit to, trying to ride the odds and read their opponents.

So what's not to like? Well, I for one can't really say I love rugby. But then, if I ever liked it, it would be in 40K format_. Other than that, as with all thematic games, the real question is whether the theme inspires you, or not. I could say that luck can ruin or fix a team, but that's a moot point in a game that is suppossed to have a great deal of risk in it.

I must admit I really liked this one. Preplaying it, the theme really killed it for me. Now, I'd really love to play rugby (in a boardgame) again!

Well designed, easy rules, and something you need no prior experience with the Blood Bowl universe even to truly enjoy... although knowing Morg will undoubtedly help you enjoy it even more :)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
As mentioned elsewhere, this is not really a deckbuilding game (which is totally fine)-  it's really more of an extended-trick-taking game, like Blue Moon or (more closely) Battle line.  

Unfortunately, it's an extended trick taking game with randomness from the card draws, AND randomness from dice, AND randomness from cheating counters, AND some random events.  I do enjoy Blood Bowl... I didn't care much for this.  I felt like my decisions were too frequently overridden by luck for them to be meaningful.  

In fact, I'd ascribe distinctly more luck to this game than I would to Blood Bowl-  in Blood Bowl, you're taking a lot of actions that either don't involve dice, or are very safely taken with dice due to skill levels/abilities/rerolls.  Then you take a few actions each turn that are riskier propositions.  In this game, there's random at the beginning (your hand, random event), random during (the dice rolls for certain actions, comparable to blood bowl), then random after (cheating).

I do recognize that if you have a bad starting hand one round, that means your hand will be much better the next round.  However,  this still compounds the problem of the other randomness-  When you've got a hand full of mostly linemen, there's very little you can do to increase your lot in life that turn.  So you're hoping the random elements don't junk out your actually "functional" turns. So, generally speaking, you're hoping your functional turns occur when someone else is having a functional turn too-  so that maybe you have the opportunity to outplay them.  and then you're hoping the dice and cheating doesn't negate your good plays.  and hoping the random event isn't bad for your team's strengths.  There's a lot of hoping going on,  just to get to the point where what you do matters.

This doesn't appeal to me, but some people like heavily overpowering randomness, and it's Blood Bowl, so it'll sell.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6

Ok, so that might be a bit harsh.  I guess this is a good game, but it just didn't do it for me.  Don't go into this expecting anything like the Blood Bowl experience of old, it's BB in name only.

RATING: N/A
Blood Bowl: Team Manager is a bone-breaking, breathtaking standalone card game of violence and outright cheating for two to four players. Chaos, Dwarf, Wood Elf, Human, Orc, and Skaven teams compete against each other over the course of a brutal season. Customize your team by drafting Star Players, hiring staff, upgrading facilities, and cheating like mad. Lead your gang of misfits and miscreants to glory over your rivals all to become Spike! Magazine's Manager of the Year!
\13\\13\
Once a manager has chosen one of the six teams, he has five weeks to groom them into the best in the league, culminating with the Blood Bowl tournament. He does this by competing at highlights, collecting payouts, upgrading his personnel, and drafting Star Players.
\13\\13\
Managers begin the season with a starting team deck full of basic scrub players. These players are none too bright and have limited talents, but a clever manager can play to their strengths by carefully positioning them to excel on the pitch.
\13\\13\
Is your team ready to compete against other teams in head-to-head highlights? Highlights are the randomly determined matchups over which players compete. The more highlights a team wins, the more it improves and the more fans it accumulates.
\13\\13\
The season culminates with the Blood Bowl tournament. After the Blood Bowl, the season ends. Players then tally up their total fans and the manager with the most fans wins the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game does an admirable job of capturing the flavor of Blood Bowl, despite being a fairly simple card game. There are only a few icons on the cards, but the special abilities and team upgrades work well to differentiate the races from each other. Just like in the board game, it's hard to keep the elves off the ball and the chaos team can't even get through the coin toss without fouling themselves right off the pitch. It takes a game or two to understand what upgrades and Star Players to pursue for each team, but once you get a handle on it the strategies for handling opposing teams really open up. It might get a little bit repetitive if over-played, (again, it's fairly simple) but as a quick dose of everything I love about Blood Bowl, the fun factor is spot on. I just hope they eventually give me some more races to play with!

RATING: 8
a little bit of deckbuilding in this fun little card game!  choose which battle (game) to fight for and manage your cards to win.  There are many battles to choose from each round, each with benefits of wining...so you must choose which ones you want, and how many forces to put there. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
What's not to love about a fantasy sport centered around pummeling your opponent into the dirt? Oh yeah, and maybe you'll pick up the ball once in while, too. Who knows?

I might get some ugly looks for saying this but, you know that game Smash Up? Well, if you like that game, I think you really out to be playing this instead. And what if you didn't like Smash Up? Give this one a try before you write it off. It's got a lot more going on than you might think.

And what is that, exactly? Well, for starters, there's a tiny bit of deck-building here. See, each game starts you off with a basic team. You've got linemen, throwers, tacklers, etc. But as you proceed through different match ups, you can recruit new, unique players to your team. Trolls and ogres and giant, spiky, rolling death-machines. You might also recruit assistant coaches that sit on the sidelines and give you bonuses, or even special upgrades unique to your chosen team.

Somewhat like Smash Up, BB:TM is a kind of area-control game, where players duke it out to win rewards for their ranking. Each of your players has their own skills and special abilities. These might help you take possession of the ball, knock over your opponents players or even cheat when the refs aren't looking!

Each "area" (which represents a highlight from a particular game) has different payouts depending on who wins and which side of the match-up they're on. This is where you get that fun stuff like new players, coaches and power-ups. But don't get too carried away hording your upgrades, because that's not how you win the game. Only the team with the most "fans" (the game's victory points) at the end is the winner. How do you get fans? Often by winning match-ups...but there are some other ways a sneaky team can expand their followers.

This is a delightfully unique sort of game that doesn't take itself seriously at all and get is just serious enough to put you into the spirit of head-knocking competition. It's tricky to explain exactly what makes it so incredibly charming for me, so my advice is...just play it for yourself.

RATING: 8
A simple card game that takes fantasy horde teams and pits them against each other through several games, (called match-ups), with varying perks to be won at each match-up, culminating in the 'Blood Bowl'. 

Managers, (players), will place each of their cards, (team members) into play trying to ultimately outdo their opponent with the numbers representing strength on each card. (Think Battleline). 

But, along with cards, players can add to the situation with the card text (team member special ability), and add in cheat tokens for surprise outcomes, and you have a super game. This is not football. But the football theme does this game very well, and it is a game I expect will stay a part of my game collection.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
2-4 players, ages 13+

RATING: 5
It didn't take us long to discover what Fantasy Flight should have known all along: The Staff Upgrade cards are game-swinging killjoys. At least FFG backpedaled with their recent [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/weblink/122211/official-faq-v1-0-for-blood-bowl-team-manager-th]FAQ[/url] and silently admitted that the cards were a mistake.

Blood Bowl's "fight for reward cards" approach has left me with a strong sense of deja vú, as I know that other games have used the same mechanic. But for the life of me I can't remember which ones.  So, to be as unhelpful and vague as possible, Blood Bowl may or may not be as good as those other games.  There's no doubt, though, that BB is longer and more random than its mechanical cousins, and that isn't a good thing.

RATING: 7
At first, the game felt like a variant of [thing=372][/thing], which I wasn't keen on as a two-player game. Blood Bowl Team Manager plays up to four, though, so I was hoping to like it more. It's got elements of area control and collecting power-ups to help you later on, so it's a bit like an Ameritrash [thing=13642][/thing]. I like both Louis XIV and the original Blood Bowl, so I enjoyed this game too but it felt a little long for what it was.

The game gets the flavour of Blood Bowl right in some areas but misses in others. If they're going to use Blood Bowl's SPLAT symbol on the dice, you'd have thought they could also use the SKULL symbol instead of a cross. And it would have been nice to have a bit more control over which new players get added to your team.

Still, decent enough for a light-hearted, trash-talking session.

Some match-ups seem to favor certain teams strongly over others, so I would recommend playing with 3.

Quick and easy to teach.

I'm hoping they will release more products in the Blood Bowl universe, or perhaps an expansion to this game :)
